General Public: ## Evaluation    Output (a) and Output (b) both accurately implement the instruction to find common elements in two arrays without using any extra data structures. However, Output (a) is more efficient in terms of time complexity and space complexity.    **Time complexity:**   - Output (a) has a time complexity of O(n) where n is the total number of elements in the two arrays. This is because the function iterates over the two arrays only once, regardless of the number of common elements.   - Output (b) has a time complexity of O(n1 * n2) where n1 and n2 are the number of elements in the first and second arrays respectively. This is because the function iterates over both arrays twice, and the inner loop has a complexity of O(n2).    **Space complexity:**   - Output (a) has a space complexity of O(1) since it uses a constant amount of space regardless of the size of the input arrays.   - Output (b) has a space complexity of O(n2) since it stores all the elements of the second array in memory.    **Other considerations:**   - Output (a) uses a more concise and elegant algorithm, while Output (b) is more verbose and complex.   - Output (a) is more memory-efficient as it does not store any additional data structures.   - Output (a) is more efficient in terms of processing time as it avoids the need to iterate over the second array twice.    Therefore, **Output (a) is better.**|||Scientist: ## Evaluation    Output (a) and Output (b) both accurately implement the instruction to find common elements in two arrays without using any extra data structures. However, Output (a) is more efficient in terms of time complexity and space complexity.    **Time complexity:**   - Output (a) has a time complexity of O(n) where n is the total number of elements in the two arrays. This is because the function iterates over the two arrays only once, regardless of the number of common elements.   - Output (b) has a time complexity of O(n1 * n2) where n1 and n2 are the number of elements in the first and second arrays respectively.
